<div id="review_1257088937" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1257088937" />
    <a title="Tanya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15698555-tanya"><img alt="Tanya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602837639p2/15698555.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1257088937?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tanya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tanya" href="/user/show/15698555-tanya">Tanya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781473200289" href="/book/show/20494154-maskerade">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1257088937" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5697147158186880646"><b>The show must go on, as murder, music and mayhem run riot in the night...</b><br/><br/>This is the eighteenth novel in the Discworld series, and the fifth in the Witches series.<br/><br/>Much like other Discworld books, it's a little all over the place in the beginning, while it tries to get the different storylines to converge into one plot—and the lack of chapters is something I'll probably never get used to, and which doesn't help the novel's coherence, as far as I'm concerned.<br/><br/>Still, there's possibly nothing more de</span>
  <span id="freeText5697147158186880646" style="display:none"><b>The show must go on, as murder, music and mayhem run riot in the night...</b><br /><br />This is the eighteenth novel in the Discworld series, and the fifth in the Witches series.<br /><br />Much like other Discworld books, it's a little all over the place in the beginning, while it tries to get the different storylines to converge into one plot—and the lack of chapters is something I'll probably never get used to, and which doesn't help the novel's coherence, as far as I'm concerned.<br /><br />Still, there's possibly nothing more delightful than dropping Granny Weatherwax and Nanny Ogg (who are in dire need of a third witch—because two witches isn't a coven, it's just an argument) into the backstage of an opera house—the novel works fantastically both as a parody of opera tropes, while also making for a decent murder mystery. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"Well, it's quite simple reely," she said. "A lot of people are in love with one another, there's considerable dressing up as other people and general confusion, there's a cheeky servant, no one really knows who anyone is, a couple of ole dukes go mad, chorus of gypsies, etc. Your basic opera. Someone's prob'ly going to turn out to be someone else's long-lost son or daughter or wife or something."</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />I've seen some classic operas, but I'm certain there were bits that went over my head—it was accessible for a layperson though, an opera-buff probably would just find it more uproariously funny. What I loved was how heavily it borrowed themes from <i>Phantom of the Opera</i>, and how musicals were ultimately made out to be the superior medium—or the one where the money lies, anyway. As someone who doesn't really "get" operas, but adores musical theater, I can get behind that sentiment!<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"Granny Weatherwax was firmly against fiction. Life was hard enough without lies floating around and changing the way people thought. And because the theater was fiction made flesh, she hated the theater most of all. But that was it—hate was exactly the right word. Hate is a force of attraction. Hate is just love with its back turned."</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Granny Weatherwax is my favorite Discworld character, followed by Death, who has a few cameo appearances... but Nanny Ogg truly stole the show in this one; without fail, anything that made me chuckle or laugh, came out of her mouth. I also really loved and related to Agnes (blessed/cursed with a wonderful personality and good hair, synonymous for "fat")—the characters aren't usually an aspect that stick out to me in his books, but Pratchett truly did a wonderful job with her internal voice, and can't wait to see how her character is further developed in the next installment. <br /><br />This particular novel was more "lightweight" than others, but I'm surprised at how much I enjoyed it, given that from my experience with Discworld so far, the books that are straight parodies of any given thing tend to be my least favorite!<br /><br />—————<br /><br /><i>All my book reviews can be found <a href="https://watercolorstain.wordpress.com/reviews-by-title/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a> · Buy on <a href="https://www.bookdepository.com/Maskerade-Terry-Pratchett/9781473200289?a_aid=watercolorstain" rel="nofollow noopener">BookDepository</a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="5697147158186880646" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1896287427" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1896287427" />
    <a title="Caroline Eising" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4697861-caroline-eising"><img alt="Caroline Eising" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1896287427?book_show_action=true">Feb 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caroline Eising" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caroline Eising" href="/user/show/4697861-caroline-eising">Caroline Eising</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780552142366" href="/book/show/802929.Maskerade">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4697861-caroline-eising?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4697861-caroline-eising?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4697861-caroline-eising?shelf=humour">humour</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4697861-caroline-eising?shelf=supernatural">supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4697861-caroline-eising?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1896287427" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11466801757251793462">I don't think this is one of Pratchett's strongest novels. There are times were the story seems structures just to fit in more jokes, instead of the jokes fitting into the story, and that led to a couple of eye-rolling moments for me, but there are witches! And as usual, witches save the day in their own way. Nanny Ogg and Granny Weatherwax are near the top of the list when it comes to my favourite characters in the series, and they are at their best when thrown out of their usual element. High </span>
  <span id="freeText11466801757251793462" style="display:none">I don't think this is one of Pratchett's strongest novels. There are times were the story seems structures just to fit in more jokes, instead of the jokes fitting into the story, and that led to a couple of eye-rolling moments for me, but there are witches! And as usual, witches save the day in their own way. Nanny Ogg and Granny Weatherwax are near the top of the list when it comes to my favourite characters in the series, and they are at their best when thrown out of their usual element. High society and culture are probably about as far out as you can get!<br /><br />My favourite part was a brief moment when we get to peer inside Detritus' head as he thinks through an usual situation. It isn't easy to write such... well, limited characters in a believable way, and though very short the passage was enough to establish his character and motivations as he struggles to keep up with a must smarter, fast thinking world. It reminded me of Grog from Critical Role - giving characters limits is tough, but it makes them much more defined. Pratchett's characters always come with their own limits, quirks and unique ways of thinking (such as the Ogg's view on possession of property) and that is what makes the characters so lively.<br /><br />Oh, and there are plenty of jibes about the opera. I'm sure I missed quite a few (not being a huge fan) but there were enough their for me to pick up many of them. Opera fans will probably be able to pluck out a few more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11466801757251793462" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13086972443417235967">I read this because I had just finished writing the fifth Extraordinaries book and I was creatively and emotionally tapped out. Terry Pratchett was so brilliant! I'd completely forgotten (it's been about seven years since I read this last) that this is the book with Nanny Ogg's cookbook, which cracks me up every time. And Agnes "Perdita X" Nitt is a delight.<br/><br/>I never remember, either, how much of a stylist influence Pratchett has been on my writing. Not the humor, obviously, but the dialogue struc</span>
  <span id="freeText13086972443417235967" style="display:none">I read this because I had just finished writing the fifth Extraordinaries book and I was creatively and emotionally tapped out. Terry Pratchett was so brilliant! I'd completely forgotten (it's been about seven years since I read this last) that this is the book with Nanny Ogg's cookbook, which cracks me up every time. And Agnes "Perdita X" Nitt is a delight.<br /><br />I never remember, either, how much of a stylist influence Pratchett has been on my writing. Not the humor, obviously, but the dialogue structure and the narrative voice in general. It should be no surprise, given that I re-read his books more often than any other author's, but picking up a Discworld novel is like seeing someone familiar waving back at me.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/142347265" />
    <a title="Anthony Eaton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2196240-anthony-eaton"><img alt="Anthony Eaton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442482333p2/2196240.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/142347265?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anthony Eaton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anthony Eaton" href="/user/show/2196240-anthony-eaton">Anthony Eaton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780061052514" href="/book/show/567654.Maskerade">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer142347265" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9717674355173251164">So, my revisiting-Terry-Pratchett's-back-catalogue continues....<br/><br/>I'd forgotten about this one, until I found it buried at the back of my shelves. Unlike a few of Pratchett's discworld books, like 'Mort' and 'Going Postal', this one had somehow failed to register in my memory the first time I read it.<br/><br/>Which is a pity, because it's a fantastic book, and I wish I'd re-read it earlier.<br/><br/>Before I go any further, though, I probably need to offer a small confession, of sorts. It's gonna hurt, too. Here it </span>
  <span id="freeText9717674355173251164" style="display:none">So, my revisiting-Terry-Pratchett's-back-catalogue continues....<br /><br />I'd forgotten about this one, until I found it buried at the back of my shelves. Unlike a few of Pratchett's discworld books, like 'Mort' and 'Going Postal', this one had somehow failed to register in my memory the first time I read it.<br /><br />Which is a pity, because it's a fantastic book, and I wish I'd re-read it earlier.<br /><br />Before I go any further, though, I probably need to offer a small confession, of sorts. It's gonna hurt, too. Here it is:<br /><br />*I kinda like Andrew Lloyd Webber musicals*<br /><br />And, as a closet (okay, not so closeted anymore) 'Phantom of the Opera' fan (phan?) This particular Pratchett title, which manages to gently poke fun at both 'traditional' opera ("another thing I can't stand about opera... are the plots. They make no sense!! And no-one ever says so!!!") and also musical theatre ("An opera about Cats?' she said, 'Never heard of an opera about cats...") is a damn good read.<br /><br />It also contains his witches who, as I've mentioned in review of one of his other books, are among Pratchett's most masterful creations. Also Greebo the cat, and the less said about him, the better.<br /><br />So this one's worth a look in. Especially if you, like me, are a secret admirer of Sir Andrew and his ilk.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9717674355173251164" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Kaethe Douglas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1072582-kaethe-douglas"><img alt="Kaethe Douglas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573927565p2/1072582.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/979032840?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaethe Douglas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaethe Douglas" href="/user/show/1072582-kaethe-douglas">Kaethe Douglas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781435274655" href="/book/show/3402094-maskerade">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1072582-kaethe-douglas?shelf=art">art</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1072582-kaethe-douglas?shelf=cats">cats</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1072582-kaethe-douglas?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1072582-kaethe-douglas?shelf=beloved">beloved</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1072582-kaethe-douglas?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1072582-kaethe-douglas?shelf=feminism">feminism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1072582-kaethe-douglas?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1072582-kaethe-douglas?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1072582-kaethe-douglas?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1072582-kaethe-douglas?shelf=strong-smart-female-protagonist">strong-smart-female-protagonist</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer979032840" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8461067251152394769">1 Jan 2000<br/>19 July 2014<br/>13 Aug 2016<br/><br/>This was one of the first Discworld books I ever read, and I wouldn't recommend it as a good place to start. There's Granny Weatherwax and Nanny Ogg (and Greebo) which is to the good, but Death makes only a token appearance, and it isn't very kind. There's a fair amount of fat-bashing, and the pretty girl is presented as an absolute idiot, and the dancers don't eat (as if that weren't pretty much a condition of their employment). Plus it's a riff on Phantom of th</span>
  <span id="freeText8461067251152394769" style="display:none">1 Jan 2000<br />19 July 2014<br />13 Aug 2016<br /><br />This was one of the first Discworld books I ever read, and I wouldn't recommend it as a good place to start. There's Granny Weatherwax and Nanny Ogg (and Greebo) which is to the good, but Death makes only a token appearance, and it isn't very kind. There's a fair amount of fat-bashing, and the pretty girl is presented as an absolute idiot, and the dancers don't eat (as if that weren't pretty much a condition of their employment). Plus it's a riff on Phantom of the Opera which isn't a favorite story or opera with me.<br /><br />There is some lovely stuff about the actual Opera House building which puts me in mind of many any old theater of my acquaintance, and how creepy they are without a lot of people in them. Against that you have to balance the business of pity toward Agnes. And everyone pities Agnes, despite her astounding voice, because there's just no way she's ever going to get a man. Probably even Pratchett realized how poorly he'd done by her, since he didn't try to give her a substantial role in another book.<br /><br />Personal copy.</span>

          </span>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_39925134'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/39925134-missing-wings"><img alt="Missing Wings: Chronicles of the Aranysargas (Aranysargas, #1)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1524456459l/39925134._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('73/KjmeNLSbWSw6XlpE0QSY40mEbWBzuqa37z+ffMovVWaNc3NPkTnFguvZhZD6e8Gc1qdXVkony071+KpzAEQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('D6CW0sZORh83uuQfBJ/GHAlhwa1TfoxuTQYMCX1Z8TY1hv8AfRCPd5CRUH7zaszD3z4mZZ3zAgkWeEq4sBoDrA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett">About Terry Pratchett</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4366413325489126452">Born Terence David John Pratchett, Sir Terry Pratchett sold his first story when he was thirteen, which earned him enough money to buy a second-hand typewriter. His first novel, a humorous fantasy entitled <i>The Carpet People</i>, appeared in 1971 from the publisher Colin Smythe. <br/><br/>Terry worked for many years as a journalist and press officer, writing in his spare time and publishing a number of novels, i</span>
  <span id="freeText4366413325489126452" style="display:none">Born Terence David John Pratchett, Sir Terry Pratchett sold his first story when he was thirteen, which earned him enough money to buy a second-hand typewriter. His first novel, a humorous fantasy entitled <i>The Carpet People</i>, appeared in 1971 from the publisher Colin Smythe. <br /><br />Terry worked for many years as a journalist and press officer, writing in his spare time and publishing a number of novels, including his first Discworld novel, <i>The Color of Magic</i>, in 1983. In 1987, he turned to writing full time. <br /><br />There are over 40 books in the Discworld series, of which four are written for children. The first of these, <i>The Amazing Maurice and His Educated Rodents</i>, won the Carnegie Medal. <br /><br />A non-Discworld book, <i>Good Omens</i>, his 1990 collaboration with Neil Gaiman, has been a longtime bestseller and was reissued in hardcover by William Morrow in early 2006 (it is also available as a mass market paperback - Harper Torch, 2006 - and trade paperback - Harper Paperbacks, 2006). <br /><br />In 2008, Harper Children's published Terry's standalone non-Discworld YA novel, <i>Nation</i>. Terry published <i>Snuff</i> in October 2011. <br /><br />Regarded as one of the most significant contemporary English-language satirists, Pratchett has won numerous literary awards, was named an Officer of the British Empire (OBE) “for services to literature” in 1998, and has received honorary doctorates from the University of Warwick in 1999, the University of Portsmouth in 2001, the University of Bath in 2003, the University of Bristol in 2004, Buckinghamshire New University in 2008, the University of Dublin in 2008, Bradford University in 2009, the University of Winchester in 2009, and The Open University in 2013 for his contribution to Public Service.<br /><br />In Dec. of 2007, Pratchett disclosed that he had been diagnosed with Alzheimer's disease. On 18 Feb, 2009, he was knighted by Queen Elizabeth II.<br /><br />He was awarded the World Fantasy Life Achievement Award in 2010.<br /><br />Sir Terry Pratchett passed away on 12th March 2015.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4366413325489126452" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.

last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
React component will render its content.
-->
